See all 100 practice exercisesLimits basicsLimits are intuitive , yet elusive . Learn what they are all about and how to find limits of functions from graphs or tables of values . Learn about the difference between one-sided and two-sided limits and how they relate to each other.Limits introductionOne-sided limitsFormal definition of limits ( epsilon-delta ) Review : Limits basicsContinuityContinuous functions are , in essence , functions whose graphs can be drawn without lifting up your pen . This may sound simple , but this is in fact a very rich subject . Learn how continuity is defined using limits , and about a main property of all continuous functions -- the Intermediate value theorem.Continuity at a pointLimits of combined & composite functionsContinuous functionsIntermediate value theoremReview : ContinuityLimits from equationsNow that we have all the conceptual stuff laid down , we can start have some fun with finding limits of various functions . Some of these limits do n't want you to find them so fast , but we 're sure you 'll get them in the end ! Limits from equations ( direct substitution ) Limits from equations ( factoring & rationalizing ) Squeeze theoremLimits of trigonometric functionsLimits of piecewise functionsRemovable discontinuitiesReview : Limits from equationsInfinite limitsBasically , a limit must be at a specific point and have a specific value in order to be defined . Nevertheless , there are two kinds of limits that break these rules . One kind is unbounded limits -- limits that approach \xc2\xb1 infinity ( you may know them as `` vertical asymptotes '' ) . The other kind is limits at infinity -- these limits describe the value a function is approaching as x goes to \xc2\xb1 infinity ( you may know them as `` horizontal asymptotes '' ) .Unbounded limits ( vertical asymptotes ) Limits at infinity ( horizontal asymptotes ) Review : Infinite limitsDerivative introductionGet comfortable with the big idea of differential calculus , the derivative . The derivative of a function has many different interpretations and they are all very useful when dealing with differential calculus problems .
